Critique the plan against the actual repository.\n\n        Project directory:\n        /Users/peteromalley/Documents/banodoco-workspace/brain-of-bndc\n\n\n\n\n\n        Idea:\nImplement a unified social publishing system that preserves current immediate Twitter/X posting, adds scheduled queueing for tweets/replies/retweets, tracks success and failure, and is extensible to multiple outbound channels/platforms with per-channel routing and configuration.\n\n        Plan:\n        # Implementation Plan: Unified Social Publishing Queue\n\n## Overview\nThe open flags do not indicate that the plan is aimed at the wrong subsystem or the wrong root cause. The repository evidence still points to the sharing stack as the correct integration point: outbound publishing is split across admin chat, summary and reaction flows, deletion still assumes legacy `shared_posts`, and `main.py` loads `SharingCog` through direct instantiation rather than the module-level `setup()` helper. The remaining gaps are narrower and concrete: the queue worker must be wired to the runtime `SharingCog` lifecycle that actually runs in `main.py`, and first-share notification and delete flows must carry a canonical `social_publications` identifier so one Discord message can safely map to multiple `post|reply|retweet` records.\n\nThis revision keeps the original goal intact: preserve immediate X posting, add scheduled queueing for `post|reply|retweet`, track durable success and failure, and keep the integration provider-based for future multi-platform work. Scope stays narrow to what the feature requires now: one live provider, canonical publication records, route resolution, scheduler wiring on the real load path, and a delete flow that targets a single publication record instead of guessing from legacy tweet identity.\n\n## Phase 1: Foundation \xe2\x80\x94 Canonical Records, Claiming, and Request Shapes\n\n### Step 1: Add canonical publication storage and atomic claim SQL (`sql/social_publications.sql`, `src/common/db_handler.py`)\n**Scope:** Large\n1. Check in a SQL artifact that creates `social_publications` as the canonical outbound table and `social_channel_routes` as the route table, instead of extending `shared_posts` for queue state.\n2. Store enough canonical state in `social_publications` to cover current and planned behavior: publication id, guild/channel/message/user context, source kind, platform, action, route key, request payload, target post ref, scheduled time, status, attempt count, retry metadata, last error, published provider ref and url, delete support, and lifecycle timestamps.\n3. Define a DB-atomic claim function in the same SQL artifact and call it via Supabase RPC from `DatabaseHandler`; implement claim semantics in SQL with row locking so due jobs cannot be double-claimed by overlapping workers or after restarts.\n4. Extend `DatabaseHandler` with queue-facing helpers such as `create_social_publication`, `claim_due_social_publications`, `mark_social_publication_processing`, `mark_social_publication_succeeded`, `mark_social_publication_failed`, `mark_social_publication_cancelled`, `get_social_publication_by_id`, `get_social_publications_for_message`, and `list_social_publications`.\n5. Narrow `shared_posts` compatibility explicitly: do not treat it as canonical and do not write one legacy row for every `post|reply|retweet` outcome. Keep it only for legacy consumers that still need a single tweet-like record, and drive duplicate and delete decisions from `social_publications` instead.\n\n### Step 2: Define a source-aware normalized publish and delete contract (`src/features/sharing/`)\n**Scope:** Medium\n1. Introduce typed request and result objects such as `SocialPublishRequest`, `SocialPublishResult`, `PublicationSourceContext`, and a small delete-target shape under `src/features/sharing/`.\n2. Make the normalized publish request carry both execution data and caller metadata: message, channel, guild, user, platform, action, scheduled time, target post id or url, route override, text and media hints, and `source_kind` such as `admin_chat`, `reaction_bridge`, `summary`, or `reaction_auto`.\n3. Add explicit per-request policy fields so caller-specific behavior survives the rewrite without leaking into provider code: `duplicate_policy`, `text_only`, `announce_policy`, `first_share_notification_policy`, `legacy_shared_post_policy`, and optional moderation or consent metadata.\n4. Make the publish result return the canonical `publication_id` alongside provider-facing values such as `tweet_id` and `tweet_url`, so downstream notification and deletion flows can target one publication record even when one Discord message has multiple publications.\n5. Document first-release scope in the contract: X is the only live provider in this change, but the service boundary, DB shape, and delete identity remain platform-neutral.\n\n## Phase 2: Core Integration \xe2\x80\x94 Unified Service and X Provider\n\n### Step 3: Introduce `SocialPublishService` and make X the first provider (`src/features/sharing/social_publish_service.py`, `src/features/sharing/subfeatures/social_poster.py`, `src/features/sharing/sharer.py`)\n**Scope:** Large\n1. Add a `SocialPublishService` with two explicit entrypoints: `publish_now(request)` for immediate execution and `enqueue(request)` for scheduled work.\n2. Wrap the existing X implementation behind a provider interface with operations like `publish(request)`, `delete(publication)`, and `normalize_target_ref(...)`, instead of letting callers invoke `post_tweet()` or `delete_tweet()` directly.\n3. Expand the X provider to support `post`, `reply`, and `retweet` publication actions. Keep delete support for authored `post` and `reply` publications, and explicitly mark `retweet` publications as not delete-supported so the system does not send them through the standard tweet-delete path by mistake.\n4. Move duplicate detection out of `Sharer._successfully_shared` and into canonical DB lookups that are both action-aware and caller-aware. Preserve current intent: primary non-reply posts can dedupe where existing callers rely on it, replies do not, and the consent bridge does not inherit admin duplicate suppression accidentally.\n5. Route completion through one service-level success path that persists canonical status, performs any narrow `shared_posts` compatibility write, and emits a result payload that includes `publication_id`, provider refs, delete support, and the data needed for announcements or first-share DMs.\n6. Keep media download, title extraction, and caption generation in `Sharer`, but refactor `Sharer` into request-building and orchestration code that hands a normalized request to the service instead of calling provider code directly.\n\n### Step 4: Rewire current callers without collapsing their distinct behavior (`src/features/admin_chat/tools.py`, `src/features/reacting/subfeatures/tweet_sharer_bridge.py`, `src/features/sharing/sharer.py`)\n**Scope:** Large\n1. Refactor `execute_share_to_social()` in `src/features/admin_chat/tools.py` to build a `SocialPublishRequest` and call the service. Preserve the current reply behavior by keeping `text_only=True` as the default when `reply_to_tweet` is supplied unless the caller explicitly overrides it.\n2. Expand the admin tool contract from immediate Twitter-only posting to the minimal operator surface this feature needs: `schedule_for`, `action`, `target_post`, and optional route or platform override, while still returning concrete `tweet_url` and `tweet_id` for unscheduled X publishes.\n3. Keep `tweet_sharer_bridge.py` responsible for moderation, consent persistence, reactor DMs, and admin alerts. Replace only the final publish call with `publish_now()` using `source_kind=\'reaction_bridge\'` and bridge-specific policy fields so those side effects remain intact.\n4. Rewire summary-triggered sharing and any other `finalize_sharing()` callers onto the same service path. Do not force summary or reaction flows through the admin-chat parameter surface; each caller should build the same normalized execution object from its own context.\n5. Move first-share notification triggering onto the unified completion path and pass the canonical `publication_id` into that notification call, rather than reconstructing delete identity later from only `discord_message_id` and `tweet_id`.\n\n## Phase 3: Scheduling, Deletion, and Operator Visibility\n\n### Step 5: Add routing resolution and scheduled worker lifecycle on the real load path (`src/common/server_config.py`, `src/features/sharing/sharing_cog.py`, `main.py`)\n**Scope:** Medium\n1. Add a route resolution helper that layers on top of `ServerConfig.is_feature_enabled()`: require `sharing_enabled`, then resolve exact channel route, parent channel route, then guild default route.\n2. Allow explicit route or platform override only where the admin tool provides one; ordinary reaction and summary flows should use resolved routing automatically.\n3. Implement the scheduled worker in `SharingCog` using `discord.ext.tasks.loop`, with readiness gating in `before_loop` and lifecycle management in `cog_load` and `cog_unload`.\n4. Make the plan explicit about the active runtime path: because `main.py` instantiates `SharingCog(bot, bot.db_handler)` directly and then calls `await bot.add_cog(...)`, worker startup must hang off `SharingCog` lifecycle hooks or equivalent constructor-owned state that runs on that path. Do not rely only on the module-level `setup()` helper for startup behavior.\n5. Keep the module-level `setup()` helper behavior aligned with the direct-instantiation path only as compatibility, so extension loading and direct `main.py` loading do not diverge.\n6. Make the worker claim due jobs via the new RPC-backed atomic helper, execute them through `SocialPublishService`, apply bounded retries for transient provider failures, and persist durable terminal states with publication id, platform, action, and provider error in logs.\n7. Normalize scheduled times to UTC before persistence and keep natural-language time parsing out of scope unless the repo already has a parser worth reusing.\n\n### Step 6: Unify deletion, notification identity, and admin observability (`src/features/sharing/subfeatures/notify_user.py`, `src/features/admin_chat/tools.py`, `src/features/admin_chat/agent.py`)\n**Scope:** Medium\n1. Replace direct `social_poster.delete_tweet()` usage in `notify_user.py` with service or provider deletion that starts from the canonical `social_publications` record loaded by `publication_id`.\n2. Update `send_post_share_notification()` and `PostShareNotificationView` to accept and store the canonical `publication_id`; keep `tweet_id` and `tweet_url` only for display and operator context.\n3. Make the delete button resolve one canonical publication record, validate that it belongs to the expected Discord user and is still within the delete window, then branch on delete support. If the publication is a `retweet` or another unsupported action, return a clear unsupported result instead of calling the normal tweet-delete API blindly.\n4. After successful deletion, update canonical publication state first and only then apply any narrow `shared_posts` compatibility update needed by remaining legacy consumers.\n5. Extend the admin and operator read surface so staff can inspect queued, processing, failed, cancelled, and succeeded publication records and route configuration without relying on `shared_posts` alone.\n6. Update tool descriptions and prompt text that still describe a Twitter-only immediate path so operators can both schedule work and inspect failure state.\n\n## Phase 4: Verification\n\n### Step 7: Add focused tests and smoke checks (`tests/`)\n**Scope:** Medium\n1. Add DB and helper tests for canonical publication creation, action-aware duplicate lookup, narrowed `shared_posts` compatibility, route fallback, atomic claim behavior, and `publication_id` lookup for delete flows.\n2. Add service tests for `publish_now()`, `enqueue()`, success and failure transitions, retry classification, and delete support branching between authored tweets and retweets.\n3. Add caller-path tests proving admin chat, summary-triggered sharing, and reaction-consent publishing all reach the same service entrypoint while preserving their existing caller-specific defaults and side effects. Include an explicit test for admin replies defaulting to `text_only=True`.\n4. Add lifecycle coverage for the actual scheduler startup path: verify that the `SharingCog` worker starts and stops through `cog_load` and `cog_unload` when the cog is added the same way `main.py` adds it, rather than only through the extension `setup()` helper.\n5. Add notification and delete-flow tests proving the DM view carries `publication_id`, deletes the intended canonical publication, rejects unsupported `retweet` deletion, and does not confuse multiple publications for the same Discord message.\n6. Finish with manual X smoke tests for immediate post, scheduled post, scheduled reply, scheduled retweet, failed publish visibility, and the current first-share delete path on a delete-supported primary X publication.\n\n## Execution Order\n1. Land the SQL artifact and `DatabaseHandler` helpers first, including the RPC claim primitive and the narrowed `shared_posts` compatibility rules.\n2. Add the normalized request and result types next so `publication_id` exists before service and notification rewiring begins.\n3. Introduce `SocialPublishService` and the X provider boundary before rewiring callers.\n4. Rewire admin chat, summary-triggered sharing, reaction-consent publishing, and first-share notification payloads onto the unified service path.\n5. Add route resolution and the scheduled worker on `SharingCog` lifecycle hooks used by the direct `main.py` load path.\n6. Finish by moving delete and admin observability code onto canonical publication records, then run targeted tests and smoke checks.\n\n## Validation Order\n1. Start with unit tests for request normalization, duplicate policy, route fallback, narrowed compatibility writes, atomic claim semantics, and `publication_id`-based delete lookup.\n2. Test the immediate admin-chat path with the X provider mocked, including reply `text_only` defaults and concrete `tweet_url` and `tweet_id` responses.\n3. Test summary-triggered and reaction-consent flows to confirm they preserve moderation, consent, DM, and announcement behavior while using the unified service.\n4. Test scheduler execution, retries, terminal failure recording, and worker startup and shutdown through the real `SharingCog` add-cog lifecycle used in `main.py`.\n5. End with manual X smoke tests for immediate post, scheduled post, scheduled reply, scheduled retweet, failed publish visibility, and delete compatibility for a delete-supported X post.\n\n\n        Plan metadata:\n        {\n  "version": 3,\n  "timestamp": "2026-04-09T17:45:10Z",\n  "hash": "sha256:e1b71f5b167354791ef58436bf1760fdef00ab35e6b7f7a066dff9862719bc13",\n  "changes_summary": "No open flag points to the wrong subsystem or a wrong root-cause diagnosis. Keep original filename but prefix with ID for uniqueness\n        # Sanitize filename slightly to avoid issues, though discord.Attachment.filename should be reasonable\n        safe_filename = "".join(c if c.isalnum() or c in (\'.\', \'_\', \'-\') else \'_\' for c in attachment.filename)\n        save_path = self.temp_dir / f"{attachment.id}_{safe_filename}"\n        try:\n            await attachment.save(save_path) # discord.Attachment has a save method\n            self.logger.info(f"Successfully downloaded attachment using discord.Attachment.save: {save_path}")\n            return {\n                \'url\': attachment.url,\n                \'filename\': attachment.filename, # Original filename for display/metadata\n                \'content_type\': attachment.content_type,\n                \'size\': attachment.size,\n                \'id\': attachment.id,\n                \'local_path\': str(save_path) # Store local path\n            }\n        except Exception as e:\n            self.logger.error(f"Error downloading attachment {attachment.url} using discord.Attachment.save: {e}", exc_info=True)\n            # Fallback to aiohttp if .save() fails (e.g. if it\'s not available or has issues)\n            self.logger.info(f"Falling back to aiohttp download for {attachment.url}")\n            try:\n                async with aiohttp.ClientSession() as session:\n                    async with session.get(attachment.url) as resp:\n                        if resp.status == 200:\n                            with open(save_path, \'wb\') as f:\n                                f.write(await resp.read())\n                            self.logger.info(f"Successfully downloaded attachment via aiohttp fallback: {save_path}")\n                            return {\n                                \'url\': attachment.url,\n                                \'filename\': attachment.filename,\n                                \'content_type\': attachment.content_type,\n                                \'size\': attachment.size,\n                                \'id\': attachment.id,\n                                \'local_path\': str(save_path)\n                            }\n                        else:\n                            self.logger.error(f"AIOHTTP fallback failed to download {attachment.url}. Status: {resp.status}")\n                            return None\n            except Exception as e2:\n                self.logger.error(f"Error during aiohttp fallback download for {attachment.url}: {e2}", exc_info=True)\n                return None\n\n    async def _download_media_from_url(self, url: str, message_id: str, item_index: int) -> Optional[Dict]:\n        """Downloads media from a direct URL to the temporary directory."""\n        try:\n            filename_from_url = Path(url.split(\'?\')[0]).name # Basic filename extraction from URL\n            # Sanitize filename\n            safe_filename_from_url = "".join(c if c.isalnum() or c in (\'.\', \'_\', \'-\') else \'_\' for c in filename_from_url)\n            if not safe_filename_from_url: # if URL has no filename part (e.g. ends with /)\n                safe_filename_from_url = f"media_{item_index}" \n            \n            save_path = self.temp_dir / f"tweet_media_{message_id}_{item_index}_{safe_filename_from_url}"\n            # Ensure the suffix is preserved or correctly added\n            original_suffix = Path(filename_from_url).suffix\n            if original_suffix:\n                save_path = save_path.with_suffix(original_suffix)\n            # else: # if no suffix in URL, might try to guess or leave as is based on Content-Type later\n\n            async with aiohttp.ClientSession() as session:\n                async with session.get(url) as resp:\n                    if resp.status == 200:\n                        with open(save_path, \'wb\') as f:\n                            f.write(await resp.read())\n                        \n                        content_type = resp.headers.get(\'Content-Type\')\n                        if not content_type:\n                            content_type, _ = mimetypes.guess_type(url)\n                        if not content_type: # Fallback if still not found\n                            content_type = \'application/octet-stream\'\n\n                        self.logger.info(f"Successfully downloaded media from URL: {url} to {save_path}")\n                        return {\n                            \'url\': url,\n                            \'filename\': filename_from_url, # Filename derived from URL for metadata\n                            \'content_type\': content_type,\n                            \'local_path\': str(save_path)\n                        }\n                    else:\n                        self.logger.error(f"Failed to download media from URL {url}. Status: {resp.status}")\n                        return None\n        except Exception as e:\n            self.logger.error(f"Error downloading media from URL {url}: {e}", exc_info=True)\n            return None\n\n    async def send_tweet(\n        self,\n        content: str, \n        image_urls: Optional[List[str]], \n        message_id: str, # Original Discord message ID for context/logging\n        user_id: int,      # Original Discord user ID for fetching details\n        author_display_name: str, # NEW parameter for display name\n        original_message_content: Optional[str] = None, # Original Discord message text\n        original_message_jump_url: Optional[str] = None,\n        guild_id: Optional[int] = None,\n        in_reply_to_tweet_id: Optional[str] = None\n    ) -> Tuple[bool, Optional[str]]:\n        """Prepares data and posts a tweet using the social_poster.post_tweet function."""\n        self.logger.info(f"Sharer.send_tweet called for message_id {message_id} by user_id {user_id} with content: \'{content[:50]}...\'")\n\n        user_details = self.db_handler.get_member(user_id)\n        if not user_details:\n            self.logger.error(f"Sharer.send_tweet: User {user_id} not found in DB. Cannot post tweet.")\n            return False, None\n\n        downloaded_media_for_tweet = []\n        temp_files_to_clean = []\n\n        if image_urls:\n            self.logger.info(f"Sharer.send_tweet: Processing {len(image_urls)} image_urls for message_id {message_id}.")\n            for i, url in enumerate(image_urls):\n                downloaded_item = await self._download_media_from_url(url, message_id, i)\n                if downloaded_item and downloaded_item.get(\'local_path\'):\n                    downloaded_media_for_tweet.append(downloaded_item)\n                    temp_files_to_clean.append(downloaded_item[\'local_path\'])\n                else:\n                    self.logger.warning(f"Sharer.send_tweet: Failed to download media from URL: {url} for message_id {message_id}")\n        \n        if not downloaded_media_for_tweet and image_urls:\n            self.logger.error(f"Sharer.send_tweet: All media downloads failed for message_id {message_id}. Cannot post tweet.")\n            self._cleanup_files(temp_files_to_clean) # Clean up any partial downloads\n            return False, None\n        \n        if not downloaded_media_for_tweet:\n            self.logger.info(\n                f"Sharer.send_tweet: No media prepared for message_id {message_id}. Proceeding with a text-only tweet."\n            )\n\n        self.logger.info(f"Sharer.send_tweet: Calling social_poster.post_tweet for message_id {message_id} with {len(downloaded_media_for_tweet)} media items.")\n        tweet_result = await post_tweet(\n            generated_description=content,  # This is the reactor\'s comment\n            user_details=user_details,\n            attachments=downloaded_media_for_tweet, # List of dicts with \'local_path\'\n            original_content=original_message_content, # Original Discord message text\n            in_reply_to_tweet_id=in_reply_to_tweet_id\n        )\n\n        self._cleanup_files(temp_files_to_clean)\n\n        if tweet_result:\n            tweet_url = tweet_result.get(\'url\')\n            tweet_id = tweet_result.get(\'id\')\n            self.logger.info(f"Sharer.send_tweet: Successfully posted tweet for message_id {message_id}. URL: {tweet_url}")\n            await self._announce_tweet_url(\n                tweet_url=tweet_url, \n                author_display_name=author_display_name, \n                original_message_jump_url=original_message_jump_url, \n                context_message_id=message_id,\n                is_reply=bool(in_reply_to_tweet_id)\n            )\n            \n            # Record the shared post\n            self.db_handler.record_shared_post(\n                discord_message_id=int(message_id),\n                discord_user_id=user_id,\n                platform=\'twitter\',\n                platform_post_id=tweet_id,\n                platform_post_url=tweet_url,\n                delete_eligible_hours=6,\n                guild_id=guild_id\n            )\n            \n            # Mark first share (for tracking) but don\'t send notification here\n            # tweet_sharer_bridge has its own consent flow\n            self.db_handler.mark_member_first_shared(user_id, guild_id=guild_id)\n\n            return True, tweet_url\n        else:\n            self.logger.error(f"Sharer.send_tweet: Failed to post tweet for message_id {message_id} (post_tweet returned None).")\n            return False, None\n\n    # Renamed original function for clarity\n    async def initiate_sharing_process_from_reaction(self, reaction: discord.Reaction, user: discord.User):\n        """Starts the sharing process via reaction. Checks opt-out and proceeds directly (no pre-share DM)."""\n        self.logger.debug(f"[Sharer] initiate_sharing_process_from_reaction called. Triggering User ID: {user.id}, Emoji: {reaction.emoji}, Message ID: {reaction.message.id}, Message Author ID: {reaction.message.author.id}")\n        message = reaction.message\n        author = message.author\n\n        # Fetch user details to check for opt-out\n        user_details = self.db_handler.get_member(author.id)\n\n        # Check for explicit opt-out (allow_content_sharing = False)\n        if user_details and user_details.get(\'allow_content_sharing\') is False:\n            self.logger.info(f"User {author.id} (message author) has opted out of content sharing (allow_content_sharing=False). Skipping.")\n            return\n\n        # Proceed directly to sharing (no pre-share DM - notification comes after)\n        self.logger.info(f"Initiating sharing for message {message.id} triggered by {user.id} reacting with {reaction.emoji}.")\n        if message.channel:\n            asyncio.create_task(self.finalize_sharing(author.id, message.id, message.channel.id, summary_channel=None))\n        else:\n            self.logger.warning(f"Cannot finalize sharing for message {message.id} as message.channel is not available.")\n\n    # Added new function to initiate from summary/message object\n    async def initiate_sharing_process_from_summary(self, message: discord.Message, summary_channel: Optional[discord.TextChannel] = None):\n        """Starts the sharing process directly from a message object. Checks opt-out and proceeds directly (no pre-share DM)."""\n        self.logger.debug(f"[Sharer] initiate_sharing_process_from_summary called. Message ID: {message.id}, Author ID: {message.author.id}, Summary Channel: {summary_channel.id if summary_channel else \'None\'}")\n        author = message.author\n        # Check if author is a bot before proceeding\n        if author.bot:\n            self.logger.warning(f"Attempted to initiate sharing for a bot message ({message.id}). Skipping.")\n            return\n            \n        # Fetch user details to check for opt-out\n        user_details = self.db_handler.get_member(author.id)\n\n        # Check for explicit opt-out (allow_content_sharing = False)\n        if user_details and user_details.get(\'allow_content_sharing\') is False:\n            self.logger.info(f"User {author.id} has opted out of content sharing (allow_content_sharing=False). Skipping summary share for message {message.id}.")\n            return\n\n        # Proceed directly to sharing (no pre-share DM - notification comes after)\n        self.logger.info(f"Initiating sharing for message {message.id} requested via summary.")\n        if message.channel:\n            asyncio.create_task(self.finalize_sharing(author.id, message.id, message.channel.id, summary_channel=summary_channel))\n        else:\n            self.logger.warning(f"Cannot finalize sharing for message {message.id} (triggered by summary) as message.channel is not available.")\n\n    async def finalize_sharing(\n        self,\n        user_id: int,\n        message_id: int,\n        channel_id: int,\n        summary_channel: Optional[discord.TextChannel] = None,\n        tweet_text: Optional[str] = None,\n        in_reply_to_tweet_id: Optional[str] = None,\n        text_only: bool = False,\n    ) -> Dict[str, object]:\n        """\n        Finalizes the sharing process after receiving consent. \n        This function now acts as the central point for all sharing activities for a given message.\n        It is responsible for fetching content, generating descriptions, and posting to all configured platforms.\n        """\n        # Acquire lock and hold it for the entire operation to prevent concurrent processing\n        async with self._processing_lock:\n            if message_id in self._currently_processing:\n                self.logger.warning(f"Sharing for message {message_id} is already in progress. Aborting.")\n                return {\'success\': False, \'error\': \'Sharing already in progress\', \'message_id\': message_id}\n            if in_reply_to_tweet_id is None and message_id in self._successfully_shared:\n                self.logger.info(f"Message {message_id} has already been successfully shared. Ensure num_frames is not greater than total_frames\n        num_frames = min(num_frames, total_frames)\n        if num_frames < 1:\n            logger.warning(f"Cannot extract less than 1 frame from {video_path}.")\n            vidcap.release()\n            return False\n            \n        # Calculate interval, ensuring it\'s at least 1 frame\n        frames_interval = max(1, total_frames // num_frames)\n        \n        extracted_count = 0\n        for i in range(num_frames):\n            frame_id = i * frames_interval\n            vidcap.set(cv2.CAP_PROP_POS_FRAMES, frame_id)\n            success, image = vidcap.read()\n            if success:\n                save_path = save_dir / f"frame_{extracted_count}.jpg"\n                cv2.imwrite(str(save_path), image)\n                extracted_count += 1\n            else:\n                logger.warning(f"Failed to read frame {frame_id} from {video_path}")\n                # Optionally break if frame read fails\n\n        vidcap.release()\n        logger.info(f"Extracted {extracted_count} frames from {video_path} to {save_dir}")\n        return extracted_count > 0\n    except Exception as e:\n        logger.error(f"Error extracting frames from {video_path}: {e}", exc_info=True)\n        if vidcap.isOpened(): vidcap.release() # Tweets are free-form: the source Discord message does NOT need attachments, and `tweet_text` alone is enough to post text-only. If the source message has attachments they\'ll be included by default. `reply_to_tweet` accepts a tweet URL or ID. **Thread replies default to text-only** so a follow-up doesn\'t reattach the parent tweet\'s media \xe2\x80\x94 pass `text_only=false` explicitly if you DO want a reply to also include the source message\'s media. Use the `messages` array parameter \xe2\x80\x94 each string becomes its own Discord message. Do NOT format as JSON or code. Example: reply(messages=["First message", "Second message"]). For a single response: reply(message="Your response here").\n- end_turn \xe2\x80\x94 end without sending a message (for silent actions).\n\n## How to work\n\n**Search first, act second.** When messaged from a channel, you see [Sent in #channel-name (channel_id: ...)]. Browse with find_messages(channel_id=..., live=true) before answering if you need context. If a search returns nothing useful, try different filters. If the user corrects you, re-examine your assumptions.\n\n**Reading further back in DMs.** When messaged via DM, you see [Sent via DM (dm_channel_id: ...)] and the last 10 messages of context. If the user references something earlier ("that link from yesterday", "the post you replied to before"), call find_messages(channel_id=<dm_channel_id>, live=true, limit=N) to read further back in this DM via the live Discord API. Without guild_id, uses members directly.\n        """\n        members_map: Dict[int, str] = {}\n        if not author_ids:\n            return members_map\n\n        for i in range(0, decimal places.\n        \n        Python\'s fromisoformat() requires 0, 3, or 6 decimal places for fractional seconds,\n        but Supabase can return timestamps with 2 decimal places (e.g., \'2025-09-09T19:41:22.91+00:00\').\n        This method normalizes the timestamp to 6 decimal places before parsing.\n        \n        Args:\n            timestamp_str: ISO format timestamp string (may end with \'Z\' or timezone offset)\n            \n        Returns:\n            Parsed datetime object\n        """\n        # Replace \'Z\' with \'+00:00\' for UTC\n        timestamp_str = timestamp_str.replace(\'Z\', \'+00:00\')\n        \n        # Find the decimal point in the fractional seconds\n        if \'.\' in timestamp_str:\n            # Split on the timezone indicator (+ or -)\n            if \'+\' in timestamp_str:\n                datetime_part, tz_part = timestamp_str.rsplit(\'+\', 1)\n                tz_separator = \'+\'\n            elif timestamp_str.count(\'-\') > 2:  # More than date separators\n                datetime_part, tz_part = timestamp_str.rsplit(\'-\', 1)\n                tz_separator = \'-\'\n            else:\n                datetime_part = timestamp_str\n                tz_part = None\n                tz_separator = None\n            \n            # Split the datetime part on the decimal point\n            if \'.\' in datetime_part:\n                base_part, fractional = datetime_part.split(\'.\', 1)\n                # Pad or truncate to 6 digits\n                fractional = fractional.ljust(6, \'0\')[:6]\n                datetime_part = f"{base_part}.{fractional}"\n            \n            # Reconstruct the full timestamp\n            if tz_part:\n                timestamp_str = f"{datetime_part}{tz_separator}{tz_part}"\n            else:\n                timestamp_str = datetime_part\n        \n        return datetime.fromisoformat(timestamp_str)\n    \n    async def message_id: int, new_content: Optional[str],\n                              new_edited_at: Optional[str],\n                              guild_id: Optional[int] = None) -> Optional[bool]:\n        """Update a message\'s content and append the previous version to edit_history.\n\n        Reads the current row first to snapshot old content, then writes atomically\n        via the REST API.  Skips the update if content has not actually changed.\n\n        Args:\n            message_id:    Discord message ID.\n            new_content:   The edited content string from Discord.\n            new_edited_at: ISO-format timestamp of the edit, or None.\n            guild_id:      Guild ID for gate check (resolved from message if None).\n\n        Returns:\n            True  \xe2\x80\x93 row was updated successfully.\n            False \xe2\x80\x93 message exists in DB but content is unchanged (no-op).\n            None  \xe2\x80\x93 message not found in DB at all.\n        """\n        if not self.storage_handler or not self.storage_handler.supabase_client:\n            logger.error("Supabase client not initialized for update_message_content")\n            return None\n\n        client = self.storage_handler.supabase_client\n        try:\n            # 1. Read current state (also resolves guild_id for gate check)\n            result = (\n                client.table(\'discord_messages\')\n                .select(\'content,edited_at,edit_history,guild_id\')\n                .eq(\'message_id\', message_id)\n                .execute()\n            )\n            if not result.data:\n                logger.warning(f"update_message_content: message {message_id} not found in DB")\n                return None\n\n            row = result.data[0]\n\n            # Gate check using guild_id from the message row\n            msg_guild_id = guild_id or row.get(\'guild_id\')\n            if not self._gate_check(msg_guild_id):\n                return False\n\n            old_content = row.get(\'content\')\n            old_edited_at = row.get(\'edited_at\')\n\n            # 2. Skip if nothing changed (e.g. embed-resolution triggers)\n            if old_content == new_content:\n                return False\n\n            # 3. Build the new history array\n            existing_history = row.get(\'edit_history\') or []\n            if not isinstance(existing_history, list):\n                existing_history = []\n\n            history_entry = {\n                \'content\': old_content,\n                \'edited_at\': old_edited_at,\n                \'recorded_at\': datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()\n            }\n            updated_history = existing_history + [history_entry]\n\n            # 4. Write new content + updated history\n            (\n                client.table(\'discord_messages\')\n                .update({\n                    \'content\': new_content,\n                    \'edited_at\': new_edited_at,\n                    \'edit_history\': updated_history,\n                    \'synced_at\': datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()\n                })\n                .eq(\'message_id\', message_id)\n                .execute()\n            )\n            logger.debug(f"update_message_content: updated message {message_id} (history depth now {len(updated_history)})")\n            return True\n\n        except Exception as e:\n            logger.error(f"Error in update_message_content for message {message_id}: {e}", exc_info=True)\n            return False\n\n    # ========== Shared Posts Tracking ==========\n    \n    def record_shared_post(\n        self,\n        discord_message_id: int,\n        discord_user_id: int,\n Parse the SQL to determine query type and convert to REST API call\n            # Normalize whitespace for easier matching (collapse newlines/spaces to single space)\n            import re\n            sql_lower = re.sub(r\'\\s+\', \' \', sql.lower().strip())\n            \n            logger.debug(f"\xf0\x9f\x94\x8d Normalized SQL (first 150 chars): {sql_lower[:150]}...")\n            logger.debug(f"\xf0\x9f\x94\x8d Routing checks: CTE={sql_lower.startswith(\'with \')}, FROM messages={\'from messages\' in sql_lower}, JOIN messages={\'join messages\' in sql_lower}, FROM channels={\'from channels\' in sql_lower}, JOIN channels={\'join channels\' in sql_lower}")\n            \n            # Fetch with pagination\n            channels = []\n            offset = 0\n            batch_size = 1000\n            \n            while True:\n                paginated_query = query.range(offset, offset + batch_size - 1)\n                response = paginated_query.execute()\n                batch = response.data if response.data else []\n                \n                if not batch:\n                    break\n                \n                channels.extend(batch)\n                \n                # If user specified a LIMIT and we\'ve reached it, stop\n                if user_limit and len(channels) >= user_limit:\n                    channels = channels[:user_limit]\n                    break\n                \n                # Fetch all channels\n            channels_response = self.supabase.table(\'discord_channels\').select(\'*\').in_(\'channel_id\', [str(cid) for cid in channel_ids]).execute()\n            all_channels = channels_response.data if channels_response.data else []\n            \n            # Also fetch channels by category_id\n            category_response = self.supabase.table(\'discord_channels\').select(\'*\').in_(\'category_id\', [str(cid) for cid in channel_ids]).execute()\n            if category_response.data:\n                all_channels.extend(category_response.data)\n            \n            # Fetch messages from last 24 hours\n            time_24h_ago = (datetime.utcnow() - timedelta(hours=24)).isoformat()\n            messages_response = self.supabase.table(\'discord_messages\').select(\'channel_id,message_id\').gte(\'created_at\', time_24h_ago).execute()\n            messages = messages_response.data if messages_response.data else []\n            \n            # Count messages per channel\n            message_counts = defaultdict(int)\n            for msg in messages:\n                message_counts[msg[\'channel_id\']] += 1\n            \n            # Build result with JOINs\n            results = []\n            category_names = {ch[\'channel_id\']: ch[\'channel_name\'] for ch in all_channels}\n            \n            for channel in all_channels:\n                channel_id = channel[\'channel_id\']\n                msg_count = message_counts.get(channel_id, 0)\n                \n                # Apply HAVING filter (>= 25 messages)\n                if msg_count < 25:\n                    continue\n                \n                # Get category/source name\n                category_id = channel.get(\'category_id\')\n                source = category_names.get(category_id, \'Unknown\') if category_id else \'Unknown\'\n                \n                results.append({\n                    \'channel_id\': channel_id,\n                    \'channel_name\': channel[\'channel_name\'],\n                    \'source\': source,\n                    \'msg_count\': msg_count\n                })\n            \n            # Sort by msg_count DESC\n            results.sort(key=lambda x: x[\'msg_count\'], reverse=True)\n            \n            logger.debug(f"Production channels query returned {len(results)} channels")\n            return results\n            \n        except Exception as e:\n            logger.error(f"Error in production channels with messages query: {e}", exc_info=True)\n            return []\n    \n    async def _query_messages(self, sql: str, params: Tuple = None) -> List[Dict]:\n        """Query messages using REST API, handling complex filters."""\n        logger.debug(f"\xf0\x9f\x8e\xaf ENTERED _query_messages")\n        logger.debug(f"\xf0\x9f\x8e\xaf SQL preview: {sql[:200]}...")\n        logger.debug(f"\xf0\x9f\x8e\xaf Params: {params}")\n        try:\n            import re\n            sql_lower = sql.lower()\n            \n            #
